D e a r ...... ,

                                    HILLSBOROUGH TRAGEDY

     I am writing to thank you for your letter and to ask you to
forgive me for not replying to you in detail.  As I am sure you will
appreciate, a very large number of letters have been received.

     All the letters have expressed sadness and, in some cases,
disbelief at the awful events at Hillsborough.  We join with you
in sympathising with all those personally affected, in whatever
way, by the tragedy.

     Many of the letters have made suggesions concerning perimeter
fending at ground, often with helpful diagrams, and we are studying
these most carefully.

      Others have made their views known on whether this season's
F. A. Challenge Cup Competition should proceed or be abandoned.
Either way it is a very difficult decision for The Football
Association to have to make.   We recognise that it is a very
sensitive situation.

     Thank you once again for your interest and support at this
difficult time for football.

                                                     Yours sincerely,




                                                     Chief Executive



                              Registered Office: 16 Lancaster Gate. London W2 3LW
                              Incorporated in London Registration Number T7797
                                             R 0 7




C o . L o n d o n d e r r y . __________ ,
NO RTHERN IRELAND.

25 April 1989.

The Secretary,
The Football Association,
Lancaster Gate,
LONDON. ENGLAND.

De a r Sir,

Al o n g with other viewers we have been a ppa lle d to see the Sheffield disaster,
and also to witn ess the enormous wave of sym pathy that followed.

I guess y o u have considered a p e rma nen t memorial   o f some sort. May I pass a
su ggestion on to y ou for you r consideration.

If in the future, some or all games s tar ted at 3.05 instead of 3.00, it
would serve as a permanent re minder and memorial to com ing-generations of the
tragedy, and may hopefully cause would be tr oublemakers to reconsider any
selfish actions.

My suggestion is that this later start could be co nfi ned to say Liverpool,
Nottingham, and Sheffield semi finals, or it could include all Cup semi finals
and finals, or it could include all matches in the run -up to the final.

I do trust you will be given wisdom in wha te v e r form of tangible memorial
y o u may also plan.

Yours sincerely,




                     my sons are Coventry supporters.)
                                      Ex,Chief Petty Officer

   He are dismayed to hear & see Pictures of the Bissaptrious      happening at
Hillsborough, 94 Killed and all those injured, then to be told it was an
Accident, Look at the Pacts, Liverpool were given less Tickets than Forest,
they were given the smaller END, So those who had tickets, turned up & went
in, as we saw the CROlDS in the Photo's, all legal,   ( I remember in the 30's
coming out of a ground after a Match, you'd lift your legs off the ground but
still move with the Crowd, Lungs squashed a little, but as you went on it gra{
dually eased Off, Maybe a women or two Paint,), But in the Case of Hillsborou*
gh, The Ticket Holders were IN, the Crowd out-side Probably with-out Tickets
Decided to force the Policeman, to open the Gate ahead, so that they could
get in with-out Tickets, So the P.C. probably being in front of the CROWD THAI
WERE FORCING FROM THE BACK, Had to open the Gates & Prevent those in the samel
position as him from being    CRUSHED TO DEATH?, so he opened the Uates & THOSE
WHO WERE IN THE GROUND OFFICIALLY, were The ONES TO EET KILLED & INJURED, Yes
as ihe European OFFICIAL SAID, It was not an Accident, People who Knew they
were NOT-ENTITLED,   turning up in there THOUSANDS, & determined to get in at Al
ANY COST, As he said the same Crowd as the Belgium TROUBLE,.
   SO KICKED OUE OF EUROPE, NOW MATCHES BEING PUT OFF, Talk of NOT PLAYING
THE F.A.CUP MATCHES,.
                        Hillsborough Contnued.2.
  '‘Sorry I wandered onto my Sports all over the Wprld, How in small Towns
still had a large Stadium, A Cruisers Football team, the Whole Town turned
out, National Anthiums, ?es South America & North, Burope, & China Japan, etc*
Yet in 1936 when I first played under Flood-light, I said they'd soon Show
Arsenal around, Yes Brazil & Argentine, have since Won the World CUP.
    Getting back to Hillsborough, It was probably The Mobs who go for Trouble
Not to SEE THE Football, all that lot travelling all that way with-out Ticket
seems a lot of Money wasted. Unless they got the FUN they wanted, after all
we've heard Players & Managers, Saying Don't play, wash it OUT, People who
Went to The TROUBLE TO GET A TICKET, & Travel, would not want the THUGS TO
WIN & HAVE THE MATCHES WASHED OUT.
     Look I'm like you & everybody ELSE, I have ONE LIFE, I've been Close to
DEATH WHEN DEATH WAS ODDS ON FAVOURITE, All my Beet MTES KILLED 1st Year of
War, Even I     I, We went & saw the WEMBLEY Wizards The WEE BLUE DEVILS, Who      h

was it, ___________________________________________________________________________
was English wasn't HE, Yes England Lost 5 - 1 ? , Hufton England & West Ham
fieal-keeper Brocken Shin Bone? , . We went to Chwlsea,     saw them play Spurs,
I was with, His CHELSEA MATES, I shouted for SPURS who got the winning GOAL,
late in the Match, ALL GOOD SPORT, me the Only ONE at the CHELSEA EKD, Shout
UP THE SPURS. NO Thugs.
         went Down iii a Sub, 1940, RST HIS SOUL.
 At Sea if any-one was Killed, or should I say all Those Killed, were SEWN
UP in Canvass, & if Quiet at Dusk, when the Bombing eased UP, THEY WOULD BE
COMMITTED TO THE DEEP, Then we'd attend to the Next ACTION. If we'd of eased
UP, HITLER WOULD OF EASED IN, Then all GERMAN OR JAP Reffpees,. BUT 1VE HAD TO
CARRY ON, The ENEMY would not wait to KILL US, TO SHOCKED TO PLAY A FOOTBALL
MATCH, how did we feel See an Explosion, Merchantman, Torpedoed, SUNK, an-otk
er The Oiler Gone, No sleep since we left with a Slow Convoy, x'here & back
Twice, then taybe 3 Days boiler Cleaning Leave, 1ES WE CARRIED ON SO THAT
YOU'D LIVE LIKE THE HERO's they'd of BEEN. ttATHER THAT THEY WERE.
   PLEASE DON'T HAVE MEETINGS DISGUS WHAT WENT WRONG, Then as Belgium Com­
plain about the BELGIUMS TAKING THEM TO COURT, That was NO ACCIDENT, MURDER,
they Don't Open Gates to let People into WHERE PEOPLE ARE LEGALLY, they must
of ah a Ticket to get there.

 After Belgium, People were saying How those Poor Chaps, yet they were Judged

Dear    Mr   Kelly,

W e w r i t e to y o u in r e s p e c t of t h e t e r r i b l e H i l l s b o r o d i s a s t e r a n d
w o u l d r e s p e c t f u l l y m a k e a s u g g e s t i o n to the F o o t b a l l A s s o c i a t i o n
w i t h r e g a r d to t he f u t u r e of the F A C u p .

Our    suggestion        is   that    from    now    on    th e    FA   Cup   be   known      as     the

                                         FA H i l l s b o r o     Cup

In th i s w a y ,     the l o v e l y p e o p l e w h o lost t h e i r l i v e s w i l l a l w a y s
be     remembered       and    it     ma y help      Liverpool       FC c a r r y   on    in   the
competition         this     year      if the     trophy     is      to b e c o m e  a   fitting
memorial        to the p e o p l e    w ho died.       Could    it e v e n be p o s s i b l e to
e n g r a v e the C u p w i t h t he n a m e s of t he p e o p l e w h o d i e d ?

A l s o , in y e a r s to c o m e , w h e n th e c h i l d r e n a s k t h e i r p a r e n t s w h y
it is c a l l e d the 'F A H i l l s b o r o C u p ' w e c a n p r o u d l y tell t h e m it
is in r e m e m b r a n c e of 95 f o o t b a l l fans w h o lost t h e i r l i v e s at an
F A C u p S e m i F i n a l in 1 9 8 9.    T h e y wi l l n e v e r be f o r g o t t e n .

W e a r e F o r e s t f a n s a n d w e r e at H i l l s b o r o o n t h a t v e r y s a d day.           I
t h i n k it w i l l be s o m e t h i n g w e c a n n e v e r r e a l l y c o m e to t e r m s w i t h
a n d n e v e r r e a l l y get o v e r .       It ha s a f f e c t e d us a n d o u r f r i e n d s
very deeply,           and we        can u n d e r s t a n d w h y it    is so d i f f i c u l t      for
Liverpool        FC to d e c i d e       if to c a r r y on in         th e c o m p e t i t i o n a f t e r
such a disas ter .           M a y b e , the r e - n a m i n g of t he t r o p h y c o u l d h e l p .

Our    thoughts       are,    as   always,      with      th e    bereaved.

Kind     regards.

Yours     sincerely,

                                                                        131 C*|Vg/7




                                          ^i,.                        County Durham

                                          j,     association                17/04/89
     Dear Sir,

                              No-one witnessing the horrific events of Saturdays Semi
     final   match           between  Liverpool  and  Nottingham Forest,   either  on
     t e l e v i s i o n o r at the ground itself, could fail to be moved by the
     sheer          waste    and utter feeling of helplessness at the.loss of so many
     lives both young and old.’
il
                             I am in no doubt that lessons will-be learned from such
     a tragedy (and these lessons must be worldwide and never forgotten or
     d e v a l u e d . ) Blame attributed or lessons learned will be ascertained   by
     the      undoubted public enquiry on the disaster and h e nce I have no wish
     to air my own views here. I would, however, like to pass some           comment-
     on the debate as to whether the FA Cup competition should continue for
     1989.

                        I personally have no doubts in my    own mind     that    the
     competition     should    continue to its conclusion for several reasons. I
     had the misfortune to be        'called  out'  to   assist    in the massive
     aftermath of the Lockerbie air disaster and spent Christmas eve in the
     ’hell hole'" of Sherwood Cresent. That, with all its        horrors   did    not
     affect    me as much as seeing television pictures of youngsters turning
     blue and dying before my very eyes whilst pinned against          a fence     of
     steel.    The   Competition must continue if only for them, as a memorial
     to them, to have it abandoned now would be an insult to their           memory.
     In my     opinion, though, this must be the last time the trophy is ever-
     competed for - after this competition the trophy should be allowed            to
     be held by its eventual winners for the year but then should be housed
     at Anf i elds trophy room as a memorial to the dead       and   injured   on   a
     long   term ’l o a n ’ from the FA. A new trophy should be commissioned for
     the 1989/90 season. I was in the terraces behind the goal          at Wembley
     stadium in 1973 supporting Sunderland, I remember how happy I was when
     the team as eventual winners paraded the cup before us after the match
     and   in the streets of Sunderland a few days later. A few of the team
     (as have previous and subsequent teams) wore its lid as a ’h a t ’. I can
     never    again conceive    of a situation that this    act of fun will, with
     this trophy,      evoke anything but pain and   sorrowful   memories    to the
     families and survivors of this disaster.

                     The  competition   must   continue, this present Cup must
     not, it must   become a permanent memorial and the last ribbons it wears
     must not be blue and white or red and white but must be black!


                      Yours faithfully,




                         mpm

                                                                                      \p L    C
     W. Sussex,




     Dear

                                      HILLSBOROUGH TRAGEDY

          I am writing to thank you for your letter and to ask
     you to forgive me for not replying to you in detail.
     As I am sure you will appreciate, a very large number of
     letters have been received.

          All the letters have expressed sadness and, in some
     cases, disbelief at the awful events at Hillsborough.   We
     join with you in sympathising with all those personally
     affected, in whatever way, by the tragedy.

          Many of the letters have made suggestions concerning
     perimeter fencing at grounds, often with helpful diagrams,
     and we are studying these most carefully.

          Others have made their views known on whether this
     Season's F. A. Challenge Cup Competition should proceed or
     be abandoned.   Either way it is a very difficult decision
     for The Football Association to have to make.    We
     recognise that it is a very sensitive situation.

           Thank you once again for your interest and support
      at this difficult time for football.

                                                            Yours sincerely,

The Chairman
The Football Association
    Limited
16 Lancaster Gate
London W.2



Dear Sir


I expect you have been inundated with letters concerning the Cup Final -
whether it should be played or not.

Surely, when commonsense prevails, the only lasting memory to the people
who died at Hillsborough is that there will be a gap in the record books
forever.

The 1989 Cup Final should never be played - either at the end of this
season nor the beginning of the next.   People should always remember 1989
as the worst sporting tragedy this country has known by the mere fact that
there is that gap in the record books.

Yours faithfully

          Graham K e lly 3s q,

                Lancaster Park Gat*.

          Dear Mr K e lly ,
                        As a membir o f th e m edical p r o f e s s i o n , nay I add my «upport
          to your opinion th a t the FA Cup F in a l should go ahead.

               1) The human race has been su b je c te d to a l l manner o f t r a g e d ie s s in c e
          time began, and t h i s i s how the l a t e s t . But l i f e has to go on.

                  2) For many y e a r s , a t th e rfembley Stadium Cup F i n a l , i t has been the
          custom to s in g Abide w ith Me. The game needs more r e l i g i o n         not l e s s . And
          t h i s ye r - assuming th e match goes ahead - i t w i l l be sung w ith f a r g r e a te r
          u rgency.

               3) It therefore follows that the Cup Semi-final will also have to go ahead.
          And it will be a very special occasion. Various members of the government will
          be present and possibly one or nore members of the Royal Family. ?he players
          will all wear black and white ara-bands, ar.d they'll line up for a minute or two's
          silence before the match begins. Zhe match itself will have to bs fought hsrd
          but fair. But, in the end, the losers won't wholly feel they've lost. For, in
          a mystic sort of way, it will be a celebration of football. And o f course
          such a celebration can only take place al:o at fembley Stadium.

               And thus - in my opinion - it will be left to Almighty God to decide
          whether Sverton in the Final have to contend with Sngland's be t football team
          or England's best football manager.


                                                              Tours sincerely,

Football Association,                                                                      18th A p r i l T 9 8 9
Lancaster Gate,
London,

Dear Mr Kelly,
     In light of recent events at Hillsborough I feel that it might be of
interest to you to hear of my experience at a recent visit to Edgar Street
for the Sherpa Van Trophy game, between Wolverhampton Wonderes and Hereford
United.
     Having purchased stand tickets (reserved seats) we arrived at the game
twenty minutes before kick-off, to find a long queue with only one turnstyle
open. Eventually we reached the gate five minutes after kick-off only to find
the turnstyle was closed and we were re routed to another turnstyle, where we
were allowed to enter and allowed into the stand to find that people without
stand tickets had been allowed into seats which had been sold to other supporters
and we were unable to get over to our seats and had to sit on the steps.
Apart from the obvious safety dangers there was also a danger of the hooligan
element reacting to the fact that someone else was sitting in the seat they
had purchased.
     It does appear that no one had bothered to have a plan to react to the
problems of abnormal crowds and some one made a decision to let people in
without examination of tickets.
     Finally on behalf of Alvechurch Football Club I would like to offer our
condolances to all involved at Hillsborough and to wish you personally our
support in very difficult circumstances.




MANAOiNO DIRECTOR. ALAN BARRETT, LYE MEADOW, REDDITCH ROAD, ALVECIIURCI1, WORCESTERSHIRE

           Registered Office: Lye Meadow, Alvechurch, Worcestershire. Registered in England No. 1263856

                          M E M O R A N D U M




To:   MISS P. SMITH                      From:


Ref: ED/MMO'B/8215                       Date:   26t.h April,   1989




                      Liverpool v Nottingham Forest
                           F. A. Cup Semi-Final
                             15th April, 1989


     In your memorandum, reference PFS/SKC/815, you ask for the
observations of relatives or friends who attended the above match.

     I obtained tickets for my                      1 and his young
son, and they sat in the seating behind the Terraces qf. the Leppings
Lane End of Hillsborough.

     They reached the ground at approximately 2. 40 p. m. , and at that
time there was the beginning of a rapid build-up of spectators
outside.   The Police asked the crowd on several occasions, through
loud hailers, to be patient.   Some fans were trying to scale a
wall into the ground.

      Whilst approaching the ground, my Cousin was asked on two
occasions by Liverpool fans if he had any spare tickets.    Friends
of his said they were asked the same question at least a dozen
times.
     At around 4.00 p.m. Liverpool fans were seen to be pilfering
from a refreshment bar at the Leppings Lane end.

      My cousin has told me also, but he cannot confirm that: -

      1)   A train arrived at Wadsley Bridge     at 2.00 p.m., but
           the occupants were not allowed to     leave the station
           until 2. 30 p. m.

      2)   Gatemen were being offered money by ticketless fans.
TUESDAY 2 MAY 1989   - 9.30AM

;HILLSBOROUGH INQUIRY

Telephone call from Supt Mason of the West Midlands Police requesting
names of FA Council Members attending the Semi-Final at Old Trafford
who went to Hillsborough. They wish to interview these members face
to face at Old Trafford for the Inquiry from 10.30 onwards and after
the game for a couple of hours. The Police also wish to interview
Graham Kelly, Glen Kirton and Bobby Robson at this office early next
week for separate interviews. They will be ringing me back sometime
tomorrow to find out which Council members are going to Old Trafford and
to arrange a date and time for the meeting at this office next week.

April 17th, 1989


Dear S ir,

I t was with heartfelt r e l ie f that I saw my law abiding, fanatical Liverpool
supporting, 19 year old son arrive home a short time ago.      This was afte r an
agonising three or four hours for myself and my w ife.   I grieve for those whose
loved ones did not come home.

I , therefore, write to complain b itt e r ly about the organisation and control of this
match;

1. i t was the wrong venue.

2.   even i f i t was the right venue the tic k e t allocation was ridiculuous.

3.   my son t e lls me that the police allowed people into the ground who did not have
     tic k e ts , in fa c t, one of his friends, whose tick et had been stolen in the post
     and hoped to buy one at the ground, was allowed in at 2.50 p.m. by the police
     to , "avoid trouble outside the ground".

4.   why was the gate which was opened or broken down not supervised when within a
     few minutes of the horror starting some 250 police officers were on the pitch,
     "to prevent fans getting to each other"? Inevitably this meant that Liverpool
     fans were having to care for th e ir own injured and dead.

5.   my son t e lls me that people who were drunk were allowed into the ground and I
     can only shudder at th e ir reactions in the panic situation.

6.   a fireman who was on duty said to my son and his friend , " I don't know who's in
     charge here, i t ' s a God awful mess".

The above words were scribbled on Saturday evening, shortly a fte r my son arrived
home.

I have now had time to reflec t and to stand with my son, his friend and countless
other grieving persons on the Kop.    I , therefore, write with great sadness, much
bitterness and deep anger and commend to a ll who have anything to do with the
organisation or control of this match, Dr. Ashton's comments on television
concerning responsibility and accountability and also the words of Simon Barnes in
"The Times" this morning. This should not h'ave been allowed to happen.

Yours fa ith fu lly




                                     «l UK. rtui                   Vj
G. Kelly Esq.,
Secretary of The Football Association Limited,

 Address



 Dear

                                        HILLSBOROUGH TRAGEDY

      I am writing to thank you for your letter and to ask you to
 forgive me for not replying to you in detail.   As I am sure you
 will appreciate, a very large number of letters have been
 received.

      All the letters have expressed sadness and, in some cases,
 disbelief at the awful events at Hillsborough.   We join with you
 in sympathising with all those personally affected, in whatever
 way, by the tragedy.

      Many of the letters have made suggestions concerning
 perimeter fencing at grounds, often with helpful diagrams,                                                    and we
 are studying these most carefully.

        Others have made their views known on whether this season's
  F. A. Challenge Cup Competition should proceed or be abandoned.
  Either way it is a very difficult decision for The Football
  Association to have to make.    We recognise that it is a very
  sensitive situation.

       Thank you once again for your interest and support at this
  difficult time for football.

                                             Yours sincerely,




                     (Signed either Chief Executive or Chairman)

I
/ / /    /              AN OlllWlllgB TO ALL THOSE PEOPLE tftO SHOULD K m ™ . •
        fa   f J l >                                          ”
  I am astounded to read in the press that there exists a Football Assoc­
  iation- Football league nemo that apparently states that football
  travelling supporters " should be co— ordinated for them to arrive as close
  to the kick-off as possible. * At Hillsboraagh this advice had the effect
  of swamping the entry system into the ground. It is IMPOSSIBLE to
  co- ordinate all the seperate private, public, individual, trjujsport, club,
  ground, police,      etc. activities into a system without all concerned
  knowing all the seperate factors involved.                                  ^ j ^


  However there is a mathematical technique,         or management 'tool, called
Queueing Theory, which can be used to measure or study the impact of various
  numbers of people arriving or passing a given point,             i.e. a turnstile,
  at the same time,      or within varying time spans. To do this it is necessary
  to know, among other criteria, at Hillsborough, the number of spaces
  available, number of turnstiles open, time gates open, time of match,
  estimated arrival time, average process time for each fan,etc. From the
  meagre details gleaned from the media on these relevant factors it is
  apparent to me that there was NO CHANCE of processing those late arrivals,
  for whatever reason including drink, if there were thousands of them into
  the *Vest Stand, capacity given as 13,500, within the time of arrival,given
  as 2:30, or as the FA-FL say " as close to the time of kick-off as possible.


  I would have expected all the authorities to have known this and delayed
  the kick-off. What do they use their computers for if they don't know
  simple things like this ? Opening the gates aggravated an already lost
  situation. Mind you, a true football fan, who attends big matches regularly,
  of which I used to be one when the City were coming up into the First
  Division, would also know this, not by c o m p u t e r s , but    by his previous
  experience. Of course with tickets you think the system can cope, but you
  lose the time gained because there's no money involved in changing hands,
  to the extra time on the journey or the extra half on the way.

  The saddest thing about Hillsborough is that the genuine fans who knew this
  would have been the early arrivals, and they would have staked their claim
  to the best view, and passed the kids to the front like we used to do, only
  to be crushed against the fence when they were charged in the back by the
  late arrivals, The victims are the only blameless ones at Hillsborough.

   I urge everybody, from fans upwards, to pay attention to arrival and entry
   times if the Government's proposals re computerised identity cards come to
   fruition, as the extra identity check must inevitably increase the process­
   ing time for each fan into the ground, and I write as an ex- computer man.
   For publication, If desired
                                                                        L in c o ln s h ir e .
                                                              Cheshire

                                                              17th April 1989

Dear Sir,
         I enclose copies of two letters recently sent to Manchester City
Football Club pic, the first written on 21st March 1989 regarding inadequate
crowd control measures at the match against Chelsea.
The letter highlights the fact that the events at Hillsborough could have taken
place at any football ground at any time. Time unfortunately ran out on football
on 15th April 1989, with disastrous consequences.
In general, I am concerned that no connection is being made with the people who
currently attend football, the so-called ’supporters’, and the accident at the
Hillsborough semi-final - they are why the fences are in place, they are the
people who create the hostile environment that exists at every match currently
played, they are the people who turn up without tickets and they are the people
who caused the problem on Saturday. They are the socially irresponsible.
The true, socially responsible, football supporter has turned his back on the
game for more enjoyable sporting events.
Every day for two weeks approx 30000 people queue all night to attend Wimbledon
without a policeman in sight, 65000 attend rugby internationals again with no
major police activity.
Please order the terraces to be closed immediately, with an increase in the cost
of admission to £20 per seat to compensate for the loss of revenue, and
legislate for all-seater stadia with maximum 50000 capacity.

                               Yours sincerely




Copies   : Mr Hurd, Mr Moynihan, Mr Kelly
                                                               Cheshire

                                                               17th April 1989

Dear Sir,
I have just listened to your comments on the BBC news programme ’World at O n e ’.
As a result I feel I should draw your attention to a letter I sent to Mr Halford
on 21st MARCH 1989 regarding conditions at the Manchester City v. Chelsea match
(see enclosed copy), some time BEFORE last Saturday.
I conclude that the events at Hillsborough could have happened at any ground in
the country at any time during the last 10 years, including Maine Road.
The conditions at Maine Road on the day of the Chelsea match contravened the
Safety of Sports Grounds Act 1975, and whilst the reply received was courteous,
with an assurance of investigation, I did not get a ’w a r m feeling’ that I was
being taken seriously. The ground on that day was the nearest to a potential
death trap that I have encountered at any sporting event.
In view of subsequent events I will be forwarding copies of my letter to the
Home Secretary and the Minister for Sport with my observations, for the enquiry.
(Although I did not mention my thoughts on how the overcrowding at Maine Road
 had happened I made it clear in an earlier phone call that I thought the
 gatemen were taking back-handers, something you would only detect at a capacity
 attendance. On a normal week these anti-social elements would just move to
 another seat)

                             Yours sincerely

F R O M THE DEP A R T M E N T OF SOCIOLOGY

INDOOR SPORTS R E S E A R C H PROJECT
                                                                                                             TEL: 051 - 7 0 9 -6022 EXT. 2648
                                                                                                             T E L E X NO. 627095 U N I L P L G
E L E A N O R R A T H B O N E BUILDING   M Y R T L E STREET   P.O. B O X 147   L I V E R P O O L L69 3BX     FAX: 051 - 7 0 8 -6502




            Dear Mr. Graham Kelly                                                                          18th April 1989


            The tragedy that befell 94 Liverpool fans at Hillsborough is
            one that has deeply moved the people of this country.
            The sheer waste of life was, it would seem, bought about by a
            chain of events that had everything to do with bad planning,
            organisation and communication and nothing to do with hooligan
            behaviour. It is therefore with absolute disbelief and outrage
            that we hear the President of EUFA describe those caught up in
            the tragedy as "beasts". That such an emminent figure as Mr.
            Jaques should make such an ill-informed statement is at best
            wholly at odds with the responsibilities of his post. At worst
            his comments will cause lasting damage to the guilt and heart­
            ache felt by those directly affected by the tragedy. We also
            feel that such a statement will do little to bring together the
            footballing bodies of European nations to tackle the obviously
            enourmous task that confronts them in re-establishing the game
            as a safe spectator sport that should now realise its primary
            responsibility lies with the supporters, without whom they
            would all have to find alternative employment.

            We ask you to use all your influence in pressing for the
            resignation of Mr. Jaques for the further hurt his comments
            have caused to the bereaved and the slur on the memory of the
            deceased. We do not ask your help in this matter by way of
            making Mr. Jaques the scapegoat for all the anguish felt by the
            people of this country, simply as the only justifiable and
            honourable course that he shMftU can take as the perpetrator of
            a gross and insulting error of judgement.



             Yours faithfuly,

                                                  18th April, 1989.
The Secretary,
The Football Association,
Lancaster Gats,
LCNDCN.

Dear Sir,

                Hillsborough Football D~i°*gter

         I am writing to you can a personal basis to egress my
disappointment with the decision taken to ocntinue with this
year's F.A. Cup Competition.

         I feel that I am in a position to express an opinion
on this matter as I was one of the hundreds of people called to
Hillsborough an Saturday afternoon to give assistance.   My own
task during the night took me on several occasions to the
Football Club Gymnasium which was of course being used as a
temporary morgue.

         However good your intentions I do not feel that this
year's Competition can he construed as a material to the dead
in any way at all.   I am afraid that I feel that a continued
oanpetition will in fact be an obscenity.

         I am writing in the hope that you will take rote of
public comment and reconsider your decision.

                                                   High Wycombe,

The Chief-Executive,
The Football Association,
16, Lancaster Gate,
London.
V2 3LW.
                                             17th April, 1989.
Dear Sir,

       I am sure that you, like myself, were devastated by the
tragic loss, and waste of life at last Saturday's F.A. Cup Semi-
Final. I, and many others I am sure,     would like to do something
b o h to help the bereaved families and to prevent anything similar
ever happening again.

     What  I am proposing is for a mass 'Open Day'   of all the
Football League grounds in the country on one day within the next
month, while the sad memory of the disaster is still fresh in the
public's mind.

     If all 92 clubs could unite for this one day then it would
surely help to alleviate the pain of the victims' families.

     What  I would suggest is that each club's ground should be
open from 9 a.m.   to 9p.m.  on one Sunday (preferably the 30th
April, 1989). During this time, spectators could be guided around
the ground by stewards who normally help at the matches.    I am
sure that most of these people would be willing to give their
services free,  considering the cause.  Also,  the club's players
should  be available   to meet the supporters and give their
autographs  for a nominal fee.    There could also be a small
practice match taking place at some point during the day.  I have
enclosed a sheet with the suggested costs for the day's events.

     With all these attractions I am sure that between ten and
twenty million pounds could be raised.  Half of this money should
be donated   to the families of the deceased and the      injured
through the official disaster fund, whilst the rest of the money
could help each club to improve the safety conditions at      its
ground.  If possible,  and if agreed by the other clubs,  I would
like the Football Association to distribute the latter half    of
the money.   Also,  I would be grateful if you could give your
backing and public support to the scheme.

     I realise that this is a vital time of the season for many
clubs seeking promotion or avoiding relegation but,    as has been
said so often since Saturday,   life itself is far more   important
and makes the football season seem insignificant by comparison.
It  is also important that football Itself is seen to     be doing
something   to help both causes. Considering these points, I would
be grateful if you could try and make some arrangements for your
ground and players to be free on the suggested date,    or if not,
supply me  with some dates when your stadium and players would be
available    for such an event. I have also enclosed a     proposed
time-table  for the day's events,  but of course,  this would     be
ultimately at the discretion of each individual club.

     I would also like to stress that I have no outside  interest
in this scheme other than being a Liverpool supporter since  1973
and an enthusiast of football Itself.  I will be willing to help
make arrangements or suggestions for any club requiring these.

     I have written to all 92 clubs asking for their co-operation
and have also written to the following :

          British Telecom,    asking  if they would set up a
          freephone donation hotline for the suggested weekend
          and the following Monday and Tuesday.

          British Rail, asking if they would supply approximately
          100 passes for each club.     This would provide     the
          stewards and other helpers with free transport to their
          ground on the day.

          Post Office,    asking  if they would supply pre-paid
          envelopes for   communications between clubs.

          BBC Radio, asking    for mentions on the air   when   the
          event has been finalised.

          The Prime Minister, asking for Government backing.

      I   leave it up to each individual club to make arrangements
for policing as I do not know their usual contacts.     Also each
club should make arrangements as regarding electricty for the day
and publicity    on local radio stations.  I would expect    these
services to be provided free of charge but this is for the    club
to negotiate.

     I hope   for the sake of the bereaved families and   for the
safety of future football supporters that we can successfully go
ahead with this scheme which would help to unite football in  its
hour of need.

     I      look forward to hearing from you shortly and thank you     in
anticipation.

                          Yours faithfully,
                     Suggested costa for the day


    Admission fee, adults      ................................       £5-00

    Admission fee, under 16s        .............................      £2-00

    Entire squad's autograph sheet            (prepared earlier)     . £5-00

     Individual autographs     (personally signed)       .........        50p

    Raffle tickets    ........................................            20p



                          P riz e s f o i r a f f l e


     Below is a list of prizes which can hopefully be donated                   by
each club or its supporter's club:

     2 pairs of season tickets,

     100 pairs of tickets for the next home match,

     5 autographed footballs,

     5 full kits in the winner's size,

     10 sets of hats and scarves,

     10 team mugs and

     25 keyrings


     The above is only a suggested list and can be added                 to     or
deleted from by the club involved.
             Proposed tlae-table for the day's events


     Below is a list of suggested tines for the day. This is of
course at the descretion of each individual club and should be
best arranged to suit the players and supporters of the club
involved:

     9.00      Gates open to admit supporters.

     9.15      First guided tour starts.

     9.30      Second guided tour starts and every subsequent
                fifteen minutes until

    12.00      Meet the players and get their autographs.

    14.00      Supporters guided Into stands and terraces.

    14.30      The team's practice match and training session.

     15.30     Supporters dispersed from the stands and terraces.

    16.00      More guided tours commence and every subsequent
                fifteen minutes until

     19.00     Meet the players and get their autographs again.

     21.00     The day's events come to a close and the crowds
                are slowly led out of the ground.

                                                                                         Avon
                                                                          17th   April       1989




The      Secretary
F .A .



Sir,
Please          Forward           the    enclosed           le tt er      to   the
p e r s o n w ho          mad e    the    disgusting            and       o bs en e
comments             on    the     Sheffield           d i sa ste r.


 I personally               th in k      you     s ho ul d     pres s      in the
 strongest            possible           term s       for     him    to    resign.
 I al so        thin k       that       you    s h o ul d     tell     the
Europeons            that Ihtey ei th er              hav e    all E n g l i s h
 clubs     back           or no ne       at    all.
 We   sho ul d        not     crawl       to     th e s e     digustingly             bi ase d
 people         on    the     excuse          that     we     need     to play         Football
 ab road,        If       that     is their           attitude         it wil l        lead      to
 no t h i n g    but       trouble         for     any      fan who         shows      his
 face     over        there.


 Yours      in a b s o l u t e          di sg u s t
                                                                                        Avon
                                                                      17th Ap r i l          1989

Dear Sir

Having w a tc he d the dreadful scenes at Hill sb o ro ug h on Satu rd a y
on television I feel compelled to write to you.           I was horrified
and saddened by w ha t I saw and I wish that it had never happened.
But it did and now, only now after this terrible disaster
safety at football grounds will be re-examined.

As a To t t e n h a m Hotspur football fan w h o goes regularly, I hope
that Spurs will be replacing the safety barriers w h i ch they
took down earlier this week.         The reason being that I think we
will still need them to stop football hooligans.              I cannot
understand w h y English clubs have not considered before the
barriers used in France w h e r e b y in an e m e rg e nc y they can be
opened quickly.         Were these types of barriers considered in
the b eg inning and if so, w h y aren't they used?          Surely they
are the safest?

I know there are still qu estions to be asked and I am not
laying the blame on anyone - I don't think you can in a situation
like this, but shouldn't these barriers be given serious thought?
I do think and I know it's v e r y easy to say this in hindsight
but if these barriers had been in use on Saturday then maybe
fewer lives wou l d have been lost if any.

I am v e ry saddened and shocked by this t r agedy and m y heart
goes out to all those wh o died on Saturday and their families.

As a last thought I do think the FA Cup Final should go ahead
as a me m o r i a l to those wh o died.

I look forward to hearing your comments.

Yours faithfully

Dear       Sir,


S e v e r a l t h o u s a n d (3/H we are           told) were             t r y i n g   to   obtain
e n t r a n c e at a v e r y l a t e t i m e        before the             kick-o

The     single      question      to       be    answered       is    why      were      they   so   late
in    attending?

B o t h S h e f f i e l d W e d n e s d a y F o o t b a l l Cl u b and the P o l i c e are
e nt i r e l y w i t h o u t blame for the total pan ic whi ch e ns ue d                                Many
y e a r s of s e m i - f i n a l m a t c h e s h a v e b e e n c o n d u c t e d w i t h o u t
of     any    kind.

                                                  15 April 1989




Dear             t C c X i ^

As parents of two sons who both enjoy playing and watching sport,
particularly football, we write to plead with you to initiate and
pursue a campaign to ensure a future where accommodation at
professional football matches is entirely seated.

The evidence is surely clear that 'standing in pens' must sooner
or later produce a disaster such as today's. The only logical and
guaranteed solution must be that spectators must have a seat, in
other words an allocated space. Of course we could do fancy
things with quick-release barriers or moats - but basically this
would be perpetuating a system aimed at herding people like
animals and such systems still have the potential for failure and
disast er.

After today's tragedy there can be only the one alternative.

For God's sake and the sake of our sons why can't we enjoy
football in the UK as a family event, fully seated as they do in
the USA.


       Yours sincerely

17.4.89
Dear Mr Graham Kelly,

        I am writing to you,not only on
behalf   of   the    many   people   around
Merseyside and England who at this present
time must be feeling sickened      by this
most recent tradgedy to do with English
football,but also   in fact because I have
what I call a simple solution to one of
the many problems that caused the death
toll to exceed the nineties.
        The solution.

         Basically I feel that one of the
problems (which demonstrated itself on the
15th   of   April   in   the   match   between
Liverpool and Nottingham Forest) was most
definitely    caused   by    the   fact   that
spectators were unable to escape onto the
pitch from the stand,and that was because
of the perimeter fencing which surrounded
the stand with the intention of preventing
hooligans   from invading the pitch,       not
trapping   and   causing   death   among   the
supporters.
         Ho we v er if all the old fencing was
to be taken down and a new set installed
then we coul d pe rhaps fix it so that each
main fence had a         lock on the bottom of
it,   inside     the  s t a n d .Then when people
need ed to get out,o r rather evacuate the
stand, then tne poli ce could pass a key

through the fence to the supporters who
could then unlock the fence which   would
fall towards the pitch enabling people to
escape.
        I have found it quite hard to
explain my idea however if you would like
any further information please contact me
either by letter or by phone.The address
is:

           LONDON
           ENGLAND


        Or if you would like to phone then
the number to ring is:


        I understand that this plan would
cost a great deal of money,but please
remember there    are lives at stake and
that has been proved.

18th April, 1989.




Dear M r. Kelly,

I agree with the F.A.'s diffic u lt decision that the F .A . Cup should continue this
season and be plnyorl to its conclusion. In this respect, I wish to surjflest to the
F .A . that a further decision be taken - that, following this year's final, the F.A .
Challenge Cup should be withdrawn as the trophy and deposited with Sheffield's
Civic Authorities in permanent memory of the 94 who died so tragically.

A new F .A . Trophy should then be fashioned for next season's competition. I
believe this would provide Football with a very strong symbol of what, I hope,
would be seen by fans and players alike as a fresh start to new and improved
attitudes, conduct and positive development in the true interests of Football, the
sport.

Yours sincerely,




Mr. Graham Kelly,
Chief Executive,
The Football Association Ltd.,
16, Lancaster G A te,
LO N D O N , W.2.
FOR THE ATTENTION OF MR GRAHAM KELLY
Cheif Executive,                                          Cheethaa,
Football Association,                                     Manchester
16 Lancaster Gate,
London,
W2 3LW.                                                   19th April 1989




Dear Sir.

     I urge you ta consider the following. After the tragic events of Saturday
my first reaction was that the FA Cup competition should be abandoned for this
year* As time went on I felt it should go. on with the aonies raised going to.
the families who suffered loss. I now firmly beleive that a match should go
on at Wembley (with the profits going as suggested), it should be played
between Liverpool and Nottingham Forest, (the two teams most closely involved
with the tragedy), there should be no winners medals handed out, there should
be no cup held aloft in triumph, the match should only be played as tribute
to the people who died and no mention of competition should be made as it has
now lost all it's significance*

     I am sure none of the players left in the FA Cup this year want to. play
on, under the banner of "Winners and losers competition". How can anybody
expect any player to play in a knock-out tournament, how will the players
feel receiving a "Winners" medal, how will the captain feel raising the cup in
triumph, how will the Liverpool players feel if they don't win the cup for
their fans, how will the other team feel if they prevent them from doing it.

     The most important thing to remember is the bereaved families, although
some would not be offended if the FA Cup went ahead, none of them would be
offended if it was cancelled as a gesture of understanding of their feelings
and some would find it callous to go on and they have suffered enough.

     Call it the FA memorial match,    call it anything but don't call it the
FA Cup "Competition".

     I am sure Liverpool and Everton can hold their own benefit match in
Liverpool as well.

     Please think seriously about what I have suggested, I know you will and
I know you will make the most sensitive decision*

     I have sent this same letter to the fallowing people:-

              Mr John Smith - Chairman - Liverpool*
              Mr Maurice Roworth - Chairman - Mottingham Forest*
              Mr Phillip Carter - Chairman - Everton*
              Mr Bert Millichip - F.A. Chairman*
              Mr Peter Robinson - Cheif Executive - Liverpool*

                              Yours         fitfu lly ,

                                          HERTS




                                          17th APRIL 1989
THE BOARD OF DIRECTORS
FOOTBALL ASSOCIATION LTD
16 LANCASTER GATE
LONDON W2



Dear Sirs,

Following on from the tragedy which occurred on Saturday
last at Hillsboro, from which I think the whole Country
is suffering from a stunned disbelief, would it not be

1).   Play the Semi-Final at Wembley

2).   Play the Final at Wembley

and instead of putting the money into the fund for the
bereaved set the ball rolling by taking the terraces away
from Hillsboro itself, installing seats and placing names
of all those lost and injured on a section of those seats
as an everlasting memorial to those beautiful people who
lost their lives and in the case of the injured may have
lasting damage if not physically, at least mentally.


It is time we stopped herding people like animals and this
system of placing seats at grounds would cancel the need for
Membership cards.

Just a thought among many which I am sure you will receive.

Thanking you for reading my letter.


Yours faithfully.

                                                                           Sun 16 April 1989


Dear Mr Kelly
I am a Marketing Graduate and have been a member of the PSA (-Football
Supporters Association).

I have listened carefully to all the views concerning changes to football
grounds, and Its administration, In order to prevent a repetition of the
tragic loss of life at Hillsborough on Saturday, and I find It Infuriating
to hear so many people give their opinions who have probably never stepped
foot onto a football terrace In their lives.

I have gained a lot of experience In travelling to see Manchester United,
(which I must point out has the largest following In British football), to
most parts of the country. I always stand on the terraces and I therefore
feel that I can give a qualified opinion on the necessary changes, or
otherwise, to our football grounds and to other aspects which would make
our No.l National game a safe place for Its spectators.


1.   Ground Alterations


I believe that basically only the following changes need to be made to the
majority of our football stadiums:




                            fWw oiJT               tarfu
                                                       roui
                       ;. V.CS& xx- p\ UarrKTS,
                      Ml Uarr*/s Its- U. doss K'.                            Insert. a.           kciue£A
                                                                       (     S£xV.o/\S>. • fk c S ^ fcr te _ .

                                                                       \ ^    ai a.          .
                           t   i a r ^ tr o^Ve_s> v>\ ^er>i»\eW‘




                                   ? \< C W
 I have already heard several people demand the removal of the perimeter
  safety fences. I believe that these fences MUST stay if we are to avoid
 a repetition of the football hooliganism that has almost been eradicated
 from inside our grounds since they have been erected.


 2.   Exit Gates


These must never be opened to allow supporters into the ground.
Furthermore, the lock must be unbreakable, it seems almost certain that
the opening of the exit gate at Hillsborough was the direct cause of the
tragedy that followed.

Moreover, the long term consequences are potentially disasterous: if
football supporters know that these gates might be opened then they will
turn up at big games without a ticket in the hope that they will get to
see the game.


3.    Forgeries


This problem must be taken even more seriously.


4.    Touts


At big games, hundreds of fans turn up in the hope of purchasing aticket
from a tout.There must be stricter controls on touts  and harsher
penalties for this illegal practice. This will discourage them from
operating and hence less fans will turn up in the hope of purchasing one
from them.

I appreciate      that this is a very difficult measure to enforce but at   the
moment it is      a problem almost ignored by the police.


5.    Ticket Allocation


This has been a^much debated problem. There are two trains of thought:
should the club s ticket allocation be in proportion to their average home
attendance, or should their ticket allocation be equal.

In the former case clubs like Man.utd would almost have home advantage
over most other Div.l clubs, in the latter, thousands of loyal united
supporters would be unable to get a ticket and so crowd trouble could
result outside the ground (due to its volume) as happened at Hillsborough
on Saturday.

I have always been a believer in the British sense of fair play ie both
teams should have an equal support on neutral grounds. However, unless the
potential danger of large crowds outside grounds can be eradicated then
the FA will have to look into proportional ticket allocation.
NB Announcing a delayed kick-off would have gone a long way to calming the
urgency of the crowd outside the ground at Hillsborough.

It has been suggested that Wembley be used for a big Semi-Final. This is a
viable proposition but the FA Cup Final is the pinnacle of the football
calender and I believe that it should therefore remain the venue for the
final only.


6.   Membership Cards


I share the view not only of the vast majority of football's supporters
but also of its administrators that a full membership card scheme is
unworkable.

I must point out that if this scheme had been in operation at
Hillsborough on Saturday then we could also have had deaths outside of the
ground due to further delays in entry!


7.   All Seating Stadiums?


PLEASE NO  This would rip the heart out of football -the working man and
his family, many of who m would find it impossible to meet the massive
price increases.


To conclude, I am often of the impression that football supporters' views
are ignored so I would be grateful if you would seriously observe what I
have said as I know I reflect the views of many fellow supporters, we are
all worried that, despite a public enquiry, unnecessary changes will
occur, and other fundamental problems will remain in the wake of the
tragic Hillsborough disaster.

Yours faithfully

        TOTAL HUMBER OF PACES INCLUSIVE OF THIS COVER «HEET




                                                                           g y g c u u m W COWflWClALWHOmiTY
We parked the car on the main road from the City (A61 Penistone Road) just before
2 p.m. about a mile from the ground and walked with a fairly small number of
supporters from both teams towards Hillsborough. All the public houses we passed
were full to overflowing and some of the language we heard was disgusting and
also very unnecessary. We had four seats in the West Stand and so had to use
the Leppings Lane entrances and, without much trouble, we walked around the
ground keeping it on our right hand side and arrived outside the entrance at
about 2.20 p.m. There were two Policemen on horses at that time and they were
under some pressure from the crowd and kept repeating "If you don't have tickets,
go away". We did not have much trouble in reaching our turnstile, C, where
I handed over tickets to the other three people in my party. The entrances
to the standing turnstiles on our right were crowded and the women in my party
remarked that they were glad that they were not having to go through that lot.
We saw several men climb a wall to get in the ground. At that time everything
appeared normal outside the ground, probably not as crowded as last year when
we were in the same place for the match. We did observe that there were not
many police around.

We went through the turnstiles and to gangway W where our tickets, minus the
stub, were examined by stewards and one c o m e r was t o m off. We went up the
stairs where two Policemen were on duty to prevent anyone coming back out, and
to our seats in Row 8, seat numbers in the mid 70s, where we met two lads from
our village. This was at about 2.30 p.m. and some of the players were on the
pitch limbering up. The Spion Cop at the opposite end looked very full, but
when I looked to the standing areas below I could see that the ends of the terraces
had plenty of room, although the middle directly in front looked full, but not
abnormally so. The seats around us gradually filled and the language and
behaviour from the Liverpool supporters was disgusting. These were mostly middle-
aged men. I saw no evidence of hooliganism either inside or outside the ground,
apart from abuse directed at the police. Several younger men had got in to
our stand and were sitting two to a seat and they obviously did not have tickets
to the stand.

It did seem as though the players were held rather a long time in the tunnel,
as they did not have long to kick about once they came out onto the field.
After the kick-off I saw a supporter on top of the fence behind the goal and
thought that it was just the usual idiot trying to get on to the pitch with
the police following him and I thought, as I saw the gate in the fence being
opened, that as is normal practice they could not get into the back of the terrace
and were being escorted to the front to enter via the gate. Then more fans
were on the fence and trying to climb it and the game was stopped and it became
apparent that there was serious trouble. During the few minutes of play possible
the Liverpool fans around us spent most of the time standing in the seating
area and any decision against their team was greeted with bad language. Once
the trouble started everyone stood to see the events and our area gradually filled
up as people were hauled up from the standing area below. While the police
were assisting in the helping of fans who had escaped from the crush, one was
seen by me to turn to the other end to confront the Forest fans and another
was climbing onto the goal in front of us. Because of these incidents, it then
seemed necessary for a line of police to be across the pitch instead of being
able to help in the chaos belcw us. We heard police announcements asking for
the Liverpool fans to move back, but it was apparent that this was not possible.
Although we did not know the extent of the trouble, the women felt very threatened
by the intimidating attitude of the men around us, particularly as there were
a lot of extra people in our row and we thought that even if the match was re­
started, all these people would be a threat to our safety. We left at about
3.40 p.m. and outside the stands several people were sitting or lying on the
ground in great distress, including members of the police forces. There was
not a big crowd outside the turnstile area and the police were trying to keep
those leaving on the move and an arei clear to allow rescue services to enter
the area.
 Fraii our observations at this and the previous semi-final we had the impression
 of loud-mouthed Liverpool "fans" who have no regard for any form of law and
 order at football matches, or any consideration for the comfort of people who
 have paid for a ticket.

 Frcm my earlier cofrments about the lack of people outside the ground when we
 entered at about 2-2.20 p.m., I can only wonder where they were at this time,
 especially those bona-fide fans with tickets for the standing area.

My wife felt particularly threatened by the open hostility of the men in the
crowd to the other team, their supporters and the various authorities. Their
        sPortsmanshlP       consideration and their intent to be part of their
 tribe with its ritualistic chanting, swaying and arm waving made her feel
very anxious. Last year some of the people without tickets who were sitting
in the stand disappeared at half time to go down into the standing area behind
the goal and she feels that it is this urge to be in that mob which caused the
  o   e at this semi-final. She also feels that the resentment caused by not
       aS "“ ^ ti cke ts as Forest made the Liverpool supporters even more detirmined
to get in to the ground and in that particular area.

An°t^®r P°int is that somehow the semi-final is more important than the Final
and the atmosphere of a Wembley match is not so charged with emotion as a semi­
final against previous rivals. The return of Hansen to the team contributed
to the fans belief that they should be in their "place" no matter what happened.




Bexhill-on-sea,
Sussex.

Chief Executive

Dear Sir

I a m an ordinary m e m b e r of the public - but w i t h an interest la football.

I think the Football Association should abandon this years FA Cup Competition.

The Hillsborough trasedy is not the fault of the fans, tt is the fault of the
Authorities, whether it be the Football Association or the Police, or both,
does not matter.

In deference to the bereaved and injured, w h o wi l l live wi t h this tragedy for
years to comc, the Football Association has an obligation to recognise this.

By not completing the competition, over the years football enthusiasts wil l
aBk ’’why was there no Cup Final In 1989’"  In that w a y the incident w i l l be
remembe r e d .

On Saturday on television, you made a statement to the effect that “this w a s a
m atter of life and death, not a question of football"., h o w can you 48 hours
later be talking about continuing w i t h the competition? In wh a t way heve
c ircumstances changed?  To continue with the competition would be insensitive.
Let the public see that you really care.

In any event the continuance of the event w o u l d   have no m e a ning    to   anybody,   I
suspect, including the players.

F or once, can we have a brave positive response      from the Football Association,
to a very regrettable and sad incident.
                                    Bedford




                                                        17 April 1989



The Football Association
16 Lancaster Gate
LONDON

I would just like to bring your attention to a frightening experience I
had at Wembley Stadium on Sunday, 9 April, the Littlewoods Cup Final.
My feelings were put down in a letter of 10 April to the Managing Director
of Wembley, Mr Alan Coppin, a copy of which is enclosed.

In view of this weekends' disaster, I think you will find its contents
extremely disturbing.

Yours faithfully




               (Miss)

Mr G Kelly
Chief Executive
The Football Association
16 Lancaster Gate
London W2                                                       17th April 1989




Dear Sir

You are reported in the lead article in the ’G u a r d i a n ’ of t o d a y ’s date as
having said that there are no contractual or other obstacles to cancelling
the (FA Cup) competition. This statement implies that any decision would
have to have regard to such matters if they were material to your decision
If this is an accurate reporting of what you said then it clearly
illustrates a total disregard of the feelings of all of those affected by
the tragic events at Sheffield.

Any financial loss which may be suffered by the FA and others must be
totally disregarded in the light of the decision you will come to in
respect of the future of this season's competition.

My own view is that the semi final and final must not be played. However,
I recognise that others may have a firm view that it should go ahead.
Could an acceptable alternative be reached involving the four semi-final
teams in a "round-robin" competition on 20th May - with all proceeds
including those from TV and advertising being donated to the appeal fund.
That, in my view, would be the correct interpretation of feelings and
wishes of all interests.

Those commercially involved in any way in the FA Cup Final must surely
recognise that the cost to them is totally irrelevant compared to the loss
incurred by those on Merseyside.
Ynurs f a i t h f u l l y

                                                              17th April 1989


Mr G.Kelly,
Chief Executive,
Football Association,
Lancaster Gate,
London W2


Dear Mr Kelly,


By baying to be allowed back into Europe so soon after Heysel and with so
little done to treat the sickness that caused it the football establishment
has demonstrated   how short is its memory and how scant its respect for its
victims.


I beg you not to take a decision now which will plunge the authorities even
further into disrepute. You must see that the only acceptable tribute to the
dead of Hillsborough will be for the records to show for all time to come
that the F.A. Challenge Cup Competition for 1988-89 was left unfinished in
their memory. Only by doing this can we ensure that they, and the lessons
they teach us, are never forgotten.

                                                                        19th April 1989

The Football Association                     .. q »pp

London
W2 3LW

Dear Sir,

I am outraged at the thought that the F.A. Cup should continue this year.

It cannot.

On the Day of the FA Cup Final Liverpool and Everton should be invited toplay       a
Testimonial Match at Wembley in memory of all those who lost their lives.

All twenty-two players should receive a specially minted medallion.

The trophy should then be presented to the City of Liverpool whereit would      be on
display in one of the Cathedrals for the following year.

David Sheppard, Derek Worlock and John Newton, leaders of the Churches in Liverpool,
should be invited to lead an Act of Remembrance before the Match, which would
include the Cup Final anthem, A b i d e w i t h me.

In recognition of the enormity of all that has happened the F.A.Challenge Cup should
then be re-named in future years, becoming the F.A. Memorial Cup.

I appeal to your sense of humanity in the wake of such unprecedented disaster
THINK AGAIN M M !



Yours sincerely.

                                                                                   18th. April 1989




        M > .£ . (sw J k fr
DearjSi6

As a parent who regularly stands at football matches with his children, I feel a sense of personal
grief and loss about the disaster at Hillsborough Stadium. I do not think I will ever feel the same
about a football match. Perimeter fences will no longer be a necessary evil needed to protect me
and other participants from hooligans. They will be cages that indicate that football clubs, police
and politicians see me and other spectators as less than human.

We cannot bring back the dead but we can commemorate them and try to ensure that nobody else
dies at a football match. Football can provide its own unique memorial - a memorial woven into
the fabric of the game. For example the FA . could decide that all cup finals should start at the
time that the Hillsborough match was abandoned; the FA . could rename one of the major trophies
such as the charity shield the Hillsborough Shield; or Liverpool F.C. could encorporate a suitable
symbol, such as a sm all black cross, on their football strip.

One aspect of the disaster is difficult to explain - why did so many Liverpool supporters arrive so
late at the match this year. I observed a sim ilar phenomena at the 5th. Round F A . cup-tie
between Hull City and Liverpool. When I was walking to the ground with my family, we passed
many Liverpool supporters walking away from the ground. We saw some queuing at an off-licence
and others standing in groups drinking beer from cans. The only reported incident of trouble at
this time, occurred when the windows of a pub serving Liverpool supporters were broken. We got
into the ground about an hour before the kick off. The Hull stands appeared to be nearly full but
the Liverpool sections were virtually empty. They did not fill up till about 20 minutes before the
kick off. As the Liverpool supporters could not chink on their coaches or in the ground, they were
ncing the time between their arrival and entry into the ground to have a "quick" drink.

There is no evidence that alcohol played any part in the Hillsborough disaster but a crowd of
people who have consumed alcohol will clearly behave differently to crowd who have not. It would
be a sensible precaution to make it an explicit offence to attended a football match intoxicated and
to give the police the powers to breathalyse people who they suspect are intoxicated at a match or
who have been arrested at a match. If there was a membership scheme then individuals who were
found intoxicated at or near a match could be suspended in the same way that drunken drivers are
suspended. Drinking before the match is a habit that should be discouraged.



                                          Yours Sincerely

C. Martin Edwards         Alex Ferguson         Kenneth R. Merrett        D. A. McGregor


                     Our Ref:          KRM/MW


                      15th November, 1988




                     Saltord
                     Lancs

                     Dear

                     He have to hand your letter in relation to arrangements for
                     visiting supporters at last Saturday's match versus Aston
                     Villa, and were concerned to note your comments.

                      In accepting, with the benefit of hindsight, that more
                      spaces could have been allocated initially to Aston Villa
                      supporters, we would like to make the following points

                     Manchester United are one of the few first division clubs
                     who do all in their power to persuade visiting clubs to
                     take standing tickets.    The reason for this is two-fold;
                     firstly it enables speedier entry to the stadium in that
                     there is no cash transactions.    Secondly, and perhaps more
                     importantly,   it  gives   ourselves   and   the  police,   an
                     indication of the number of visiting supporters attending.
                     In   that   way,  the    appropriate    amount   of   terraced
                     accommodation can be reserved and an adequate number of
                     turnstiles provided.

                     On approaching Aston Villa, they advised that they required
                     1,000 terraced tickets and these were duly despatched.
                     Just five days before the match, Aston Villa requested
                     another 500 tickets.   We then contacted them two days prior
                     to the match only to be told that they had sold out the
                     previous evening.   In any event, there were 4,362 visiting
                     supporters and the terrace spaces allocated to them has a
                     capacity of 4,550.   We are accepting the criticism that the
                     packing might have been better but in view of the advanced
                     sales to visiting supporters, we had absolutely no way of
                     knowing that such a large number of non-ticket holders
                     would   arrive   and    it  would   therefore,   have    been
                     inappropriate to pack early arrivals as tightly as one
                     would when capacity in that section was expected to be
                     achieved.    Problems were     also  compounded  by   traffic
                     congestions and we know that six or seven coaches did not
                     arrive at the stadium until 10 minutes after kick-off.



President: Sir Matt Busby CBE.
Directors: C M. Edwards (Chairman), J.M. Edelson, R. Charlton CBE, E.M. Watkins, A M Al Midani, N. Burrows. R.L. Olive.

Chief Executive            Manager              Secretary                  Commercial Manager
C. Martin Edwards          Alex Ferguson        Kenneth R. Merrett         D. A. McGregor




                     The above information should not be seen as criticism of
                     Aston Villa Football Club.  They have to make an assessment
                     of the number of tickets they expect to sell and there is
                     the fact that very many football supporters refuse to
                     purchase tickets in advance.   This, in turn, leads to the
                     kind of problems experienced last Saturday.

                      Whilst also accepting that it may have seemed that the
                      police were 'slow to react' by opening additional sections,
                      it should be borne in mind that police officers on duty in
                      and around the stadium have specific tasks to perform and
                      it can take a little time and some 'juggling' in order to
                      arrange for an orderly and safe movement of spectators
                      without weakening other areas.

                      I  do hope that this information helps to clarify the
                      situation and I thank you for taking the trouble to write,
                      thus giving us the opportunity to explain our actions.

                      Yours sincerely.




                      K.R. Merrett,
                      Secretary

                                                      Your reference
                                                      Our reference    AER/JEP
                                                      Date             8 December 1988


         SALFORD.

                                              J




     Dear Mr.

     I reply to your letter of the 7th November 1988 following your visit
     to Manchester United football stadium when Manchester United played
     Aston Villa.   Your main criticism is regarding the segregation and the
     way that supporters were inadequately housed in the terraced area of
     the ground.

     As you may be aware, the ground attendance that day was 44,804 and of
     those, 4,500 were Aston Villa supporters.   Prior to the game the
     intelligence received from the home supporters club was that visitors
     would be in the region of 2-3,000.     It was only based on our experience
     over previous seasons that we allowed extra areas to accommodate any extra
     casual supporters who might have arrived.

     As a result of this we were able, albeit in a somewhat confined area, to
     accommodate nearly twice the number of visitors anticipated.

     Before and during the match police officers attempted, not always
     successfully, to ensure that the Aston Villa fans moved towards the front
     of the terraced areas and I can assure you that irrespective of where you
     were standing or how tightly packed it may have been, each of the areas in
     question was not filled to capacity.

     I am not aware of the specific incident you identify in your letter of the
     gentleman and his wife, but to date I have received no other letters of
     complaint in respect of these matters.

     I accept the incident with the firework prior to the game but I am sure you
     will appreciate that with crowds in such numbers coming into the stadium
     officers who are searching on a random basis have to rely on experience
     and such crowds, particularly arriving at the last minute as invariably
     they do, are not conducive to finding small items such as fireworks being
     brought in.



                                                                              contd
                             -   2   -




I thank you for your letter as I am always aware that any criticism
must be looked at constructively, and as such we will endeavour, as
we always do, to improve and ensure that Old Trafford remains one of
the safest stadia in England.




                           Yours sincerely,




                                 Chief Superintendent

 Our Ref:    RHGK/MMO' B/8196                  Your Ref:

                                                                                      24th April,       1989




    Sussex




    Dear Mr.

                                      HILLSBOROUGH TRAGEDY

         I      am writing to thank you for your letter and to ask
    you to forgive me for not replying to you in detail.   As I
    am sure you will appreciate, a very large number of letters
    have been received.

         All the letters have expressed sadness and, in some
    cases, disbelief at the awful events at Hillsborough.   We
    join with you in sympathising with all those personally
    affected, in whatever way, by the tragedy.

         Many of the letters have made suggestions concerning
    perimeter fencing at grounds, often with helpful diagrams,
    and we are studying these most carefully.

         Others have made their views known on whether this
    Season's F. A. Challenge Cup Competition should proceed or
    be abandoned.   Either way it is a very difficult decision
    for The Football Association to have to make.    We
    recognise that it is a very sensitive situation.

         Thank you once again for your interest and support
    at this difficult time for football.

                                                           Yours sincerely.



                                                                        Executive



                                Registered Office: 16 Lancaster Gate, London W2 3LW
                                Incorporated in London Registration Number 77797
